Question: 138
9.  Here are two possible algorithms for shuffling the deck.   Algorithm 1   Initialize an array of  Card  called  shuffled  of length  NUMCARDS .  Set  k  to  0 .  For  j=0  to  NUMCARDS/2-1   - Copy  cards[j]  to  shuffled[k]   - Set  k  to  k+2   Set  k  to  1 .  For  j=NUMCARDS/2  to  NUMCARDS-1   - Copy  cards[j]  to  shuffled[k]   - Set  k  to  k+2    Algorithm 2   Initialize an array of  Card  called  shuffled  containing  NUMCARDS  slots.  For  k=0  to  NUMCARDS-1   - Repeatedly generate a random integer  j  from  0  to  NUMCARDS-1 , until  cards[j]  contains a card not marked as empty  - Copy  cards[j]  to  shuffled[k]   - Set  cards[j]  to empty  Which is a false statement concerning Algorithms 1 and 2?
A. A disadvantage of Algorithm 1 is that it wonât generate all possible deck permutations.  B. For Algorithm 2, to determine the last element shuffled requires an average of  NUMCARDS  calls to the random number generator.  C. Algorithm 2 will lead to more permutations of the deck than Algorithm 1.  D. In terms of run time, Algorithm 2 is more efficient than Algorithm 1.  E. If Algorithm 1 is repeated several times, it may return the deck to its original state.
Correct Answer:  D
Explanation:
The big defect of Algorithm 2 is that it eventually slows down. This is because every time it selects an empty element, it has to loop again. Each of the other choices is true. In choice A, for example, the element  cards[0]  always moves to  shuffled[0] , eliminating all permutations that have  cards[0]  in a different slot. For choice B, by the time you get to assign the last element, all but two slots of the  cards  array are marked empty. So, on average, you will need to go through  NUMCARDS  tries to find one of those two nonempty slots. For choice C, even though Algorithm 2 is slow, in theory every element in  cards  could land in any given slot in  shuffled . This is not true for Algorithm 1, where the first element never budges out of the first slot. For choice E, because of the precise ordering of elements in Algorithm 1, the array will always eventually return to its original state, assuming there are sufficient iterations.

Consider the following method.  <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/p0291-01.jpg"/>  If the current state of a matrix  mat  is  <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/p0291-02.jpg"/>  which matrix will result from the method call  alterArray(mat[2]) ?
A. <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/p0291-03.jpg"/>  B. <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/p0291-04.jpg"/>  C. <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/p0291-05.jpg"/>  D. <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/p0291-06.jpg"/>  E. <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/p0291-07.jpg"/>
Correct Answer:  D
Explanation:

The method  alterArray  swaps the first and last elements of an array, then the second and second-last elements, and so on, until it reaches the middle of the array. The method call  alterArray(mat[2])  performs this series of swaps on row 2 of the matrix, the bottom row, resulting in the matrix in choice D.

Question: 154
5.  The method  changeNegs  below should replace every occurrence of a negative integer in its matrix parameter with 0.  <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/p0292-01.jpg"/>  Which is a correct replacement for  /*  <i> code </i>  */ ?  I. <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/p0292-02.jpg"/>  II. <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/p0292-03.jpg"/>  III. <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/p0292-04.jpg"/>
A. I only  B. II only  C. III only  D. I and II only  E. I, II, and III
Correct Answer:  D
Explanation:
Segment I is a row-by-row traversal; segment II is a column-by-column traversal. Each achieves the correct postcondition. Segment III traverses the matrix but does not alter it. All that is changed is the local variable  element . You cannot use this kind of loop to replace elements in an array.

Question: 159
10.  Consider a square matrix in a class that has a private instance variable  mat .   private int[][] mat;   Method  alter  in the class changes  mat .  <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/p0298-02.jpg"/>  If  mat  has current value  <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/p0298-03.jpg"/>  what are the contents of  mat  after method  alter  has been executed?
A. <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/p0298-04.jpg"/>  B. <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/p0298-05.jpg"/>  C. <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/p0298-06.jpg"/>  D. <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/p0298-07.jpg"/>  E. <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/p0298-08.jpg"/>
Correct Answer:  A
Explanation:
Method  alter  places a mirror along the major diagonal and reflects the elements from left to right across this diagonal.  <img alt="Images" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/p0307-02.jpg"/>  In this algorithm, when  row  is  1, col  can only be  0 , and when  row  is  2, col  takes on the values  0  and  1 . Thus, only three elements are altered:  mat[0][1], mat[0][2] , and  mat[1][2] . (Note that the method assigns values to  mat[col][row] .) These elements are all to the right of the diagonal. Choice A is the only choice that leaves elements to the left of the diagonal unchanged.

Question: 161
1.  Which of the following statements about recursion are true?  I. Every recursive algorithm can be written iteratively.  II. Tail recursion is always used in "divide-and-conquer" algorithms.  III. In a recursive definition, a process is defined in terms of a simpler case of itself.
A. I only  B. III only  C. I and II only  D. I and III only  E. II and III only
Correct Answer:  D
Explanation:
Tail recursion is when the recursive call of a method is made as the last executable step of the method. Divide-and-conquer algorithms like those used in merge sort or quicksort have recursive calls <i>before</i> the last step. Thus, statement II is false.

Question: 163
3.  Refer to the method  stringRecur .  <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/p0327-01.jpg"/>  When will method  stringRecur  terminate without error?
A. Only when the length of the input string is less than 15  B. Only when the length of the input string is greater than or equal to 15  C. Only when an empty string is input  D. For all string inputs  E. For no string inputs
Correct Answer:  E
Explanation:
When  stringRecur  is invoked, it calls itself irrespective of the length of  s . Since there is no action that leads to termination, the method will not terminate until the computer runs out of memory (run-time error).

Question: 166
6.  If <i>n</i> &gt; 0, how many times will  result  be called to evaluate  result(n)  (including the initial call)?
A. 2  B. 2<i><sup>n</sup></i>  C. <i>n</i>  D. 2<i>n</i>  E. <i>n</i><sup>2</sup>
Correct Answer:  C
Explanation:
For  result(n)  there will be (<i>n</i> ? 1) recursive calls before  result(1) , the base case, is reached. Adding the initial call gives a total of <i>n</i> method calls.

Correct Answer:  D
Explanation:

Question: 169
9.  What does method  recur  do?  <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/p0329-01.jpg"/>
A. It finds the largest value in  x  and leaves  x  unchanged.  B. It finds the smallest value in  x  and leaves  x  unchanged.  C. It sorts  x  in ascending order and returns the largest value in  x .  D. It sorts  x  in descending order and returns the largest value in  x .  E. It returns  x[0]  or  x[n-1] , whichever is larger.
Correct Answer:  A
Explanation:
If there is only one element in  x , then  recur  returns that element. Having the recursive call at the beginning of the  else  part of the algorithm causes the  if  part for each method call to be stacked until  t  eventually gets assigned to  x[0] . The pending  if  statements are then executed, and  t  is compared to each element in  x . The largest value in  x  is returned.
#########################################################

Correct Answer:  B
Explanation:
Since the recursive call is made directly following the base case, the  System.out.printâ¦  statements are stacked up. If  printString("cat")  is called, here is the sequence of recursive calls and pending statements on the stack:  <img alt="Images" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/p0338-01.jpg"/>  When  printString("") , the base case, is called, the  print  statements are then popped off the stack in reverse order, which means that the characters of the string will be printed in reverse order.

Question: 173
3.  A user enters several positive integers at the keyboard and terminates the list with a sentinel ( -999 ). A  writeEven  method reads those integers and outputs the even integers only, in the reverse order that they are read. Thus, if the user enters   3 5 14 6 1 8 -999   the output for the  writeEven  method will be   8 6 14   Assume that the user enters at least one positive integer and terminates the list with â999. Here is the method.  <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/p0331-01.jpg"/>  Which  /*  <i> code </i>  */  satisfies the postcondition of method  writeEven ?  I. <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/p0331-02.jpg"/>  II. <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/p0331-03.jpg"/>  III. <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/p0331-04.jpg"/>
A. I only  B. II only  C. III only  D. I and II only  E. I, II, and III
Correct Answer:  C
Explanation:
Since even numbers are printed <i>before</i> the recursive call in segment I, they will be printed in the order in which they are read from the keyboard. Contrast this with the correct choice, segment III, in which the recursive call is made before the test for evenness. These tests will be stacked until the last number is read. Recall that the pending statements are removed from the stack in reverse order (most recent recursive call first), which leads to even numbers being printed in reverse order. Segment II is wrong because all numbers entered will be printed, irrespective of whether they are even or not. Note that segment II would work if the input list contained only even numbers.

This is a base case, so  365  will be written out, resulting in  051,365 . A number like 278278 (two sets of three identical digits) will be written out correctly, as will a "symmetrical" number like 251462251. Also, any <i>n</i> &lt; 1000 is a base case and the number will be written out correctly as is.

Question: 183
2.  The following code fragment does a sequential search to determine whether a given integer,  value , is stored in an array  a[0]  â¦  a[n-1] .  <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/p0352-01.jpg"/>  Which of the following should replace  /*  <i> boolean expression </i>  */  so that the algorithm works as intended?

Correct Answer:  D
Explanation:
Choice B doesnât make sense: The loop will be exited as soon as a value is found that does <i>not</i> equal  a[i] . Question: 185
4.  Array  unsortedArr  contains an unsorted list of integers. Array  sortedArr  contains a list of integers sorted in increasing order. Which of the following operations is more efficient for  sortedArr  than  unsortedArr ? Assume the most efficient algorithms are used.  I. Inserting a new element  II. Searching for a given element  III. Computing the mean of the elements
A. I only  B. II only  C. III only  D. I and II only  E. I, II, and III
Correct Answer:  B
Explanation:
Inserting a new element is quick and easy in an unsorted arrayâjust add it to the end of the list. Computing the mean involves finding the sum of the elements and dividing by <i>n</i>, the number of elements. The execution time is the same whether the list is sorted or not. Operation II, searching, is inefficient for an unsorted list, since a sequential search must be used. In  sortedArr , the efficient binary search algorithm, which involves fewer comparisons, could be used. In fact, in a sorted list, even a sequential search would be more efficient than for an unsorted list: If the search item were not in the list, the search could stop as soon as the list elements were greater than the search item.

Correct Answer:  B
Explanation:

Using the general rule for finding the number of iterations when  key  is not in the list: If <i>n</i> is the number of elements, round <i>n</i> up to the nearest power of 2, which is 8 in this case. Question: 196
6.  A large sorted array containing about 30,000 elements is to be searched for a value  key  using an iterative binary search algorithm. Assuming that  key  is in the array, which of the following is closest to the smallest number of iterations that will guarantee that  key  is found? Note: 10<sup>3</sup> â 2<sup>10</sup>.
A. 15  B. 30  C. 100  D. 300  E. 3000
Correct Answer:  A
Explanation:
30,000 = 1000 Ã 30 â 2<sup>10</sup> Ã 2<sup>5</sup> = 2<sup>15</sup>. Since a successful binary search in the worst case requires log<sub>2</sub> <i>n</i> iterations, 15 iterations will guarantee that  key  is found. (Note that 30,000 &lt; 2<sup>10</sup> Ã 2<sup>5</sup> = 32,768.) Shortcut: 30,000 &lt; 2<sup>15</sup>. Therefore, the maximum (worst case) number of comparisons that guarantees the key is found is equal to the exponent, 15.

Question: 198
8.  When sorted biggest to smallest with  insertionSort , which list will need the fewest changes of position for individual elements?
A. 5, 1, 2, 3, 4, 9  B. 9, 5, 1, 4, 3, 2  C. 9, 4, 2, 5, 1, 3  D. 9, 3, 5, 1, 4, 2  E. 3, 2, 1, 9, 5, 4
Correct Answer:  B
Explanation:
An insertion sort compares  a[1]  and  a[0] . If they are not in the correct order,  a[0]  is moved and  a[1]  is inserted in its correct position.  a[2]  is then inserted in its correct position, and  a[0]  and  a[1]  are moved if necessary, and so on. Since B has only one element out of order, it will require the fewest changes.

Question: 200
10.  While typing the  insertionSort  method, a programmer by mistake enters   while (temp &gt; a[j])   instead of   while (j &gt;= 0 &amp;&amp; temp &gt; a[j])   Despite this mistake, the method works as intended the first time the programmer enters an array to be sorted in descending order. Which of the following could explain this?  I. The first element in the array was the largest element in the array.  II. The array was already sorted in descending order.  III. A. I only  B. II only  C. III only  D. I and II only  E. II and III only
Correct Answer:  D
Explanation:
j &gt;= 0  is a stopping condition that prevents an element that is larger than all those to the left of it from going off the left end of the array. If no error occurred, it means that the largest element in the array was  a[0] , which was true in situations I and II. Question: 201
1.  The elements in a long list of integers are roughly sorted in decreasing order. No more than 5 percent of the elements are out of order. Which of the following is a valid reason for using an insertion sort rather than a selection sort to sort this list into decreasing order?  I. There will be fewer comparisons of elements for insertion sort.  II. There will be fewer changes of position of elements for insertion sort.  III. There will be less space required for insertion sort.
A. I only  B. II only  C. III only  D. I and II only  E. I, II, and III
Correct Answer:  A
Explanation:
Look at a small array that is almost sorted:  10 8 9 6 2  For <span class="underline">insertion sort</span>, you need four passes through this array.  The first pass compares 8 and 10âone comparison, no moves.  The second pass compares 9 and 8, then 9 and 10. The array becomes 10 9 8 6 2âtwo comparisons, two moves.  The third and fourth passes compare 6 and 8, and 2 and 6âno moves.  In summary, there are approximately one or two comparisons per pass and no more than two moves per pass.  For <span class="underline">selection sort</span>, there are four passes too.  The first pass finds the biggest element in the array and swaps it into the first position.  The array is still 10 8 9 6 2âfour comparisons. There are two moves if your algorithm makes the swap in this case, otherwise no moves.  The second pass finds the biggest element from  a[1]  to  a[4]  and swaps it into the second position: 10 9 8 6 2âthree comparisons, two moves.  For the third pass there are two comparisons, and one for the fourth. There are zero or two moves each time.  Summary: 4 + 3 + 2 + 1 total comparisons and a possible two moves per pass.  Notice that reason I is valid. Selection sort makes the same number of comparisons irrespective of the state of the array. Insertion sort does far fewer comparisons if the array is almost sorted. Reason II is invalid. There are roughly the same number of data movements for insertion and selection. Insertion may even have more changes, depending on how far from their insertion points the unsorted elements are. Reason III is wrong because insertion and selection sorts have the same space requirements.
#########################################################
Question: 202
2.  Which of the following is a valid reason why merge sort is a better sorting algorithm than insertion sort for sorting long, randomly ordered lists?  I. Merge sort requires less code than insertion sort.  II. Merge sort requires less storage space than insertion sort.  III. Merge sort runs faster than insertion sort.
A. I only  B. II only  C. III only  D. I and II only  E. II and III only
Correct Answer:  C
Explanation:
Reject reason I. Merge sort requires both a  merge  and a  mergeSort  methodâ<i>more</i> code than the relatively short and simple code for insertion sort. Reject reason II. The  merge  algorithm uses a temporary array, which means <i>more</i> storage space than insertion sort. Reason III is correct. For long lists, the "divide-and-conquer" approach of merge sort gives it a faster run time than insertion sort.

Question: 203
3.  A large array of lowercase characters is to be searched for the pattern "pqrs." The first step in a very efficient searching algorithm is to look at characters with index
A. 0, 1, 2, â¦ until a "p" is encountered.  B. 0, 1, 2, â¦ until any letter in "p" â¦ "s" is encountered.  C. 3, 7, 11, â¦ until an "s" is encountered.  D. 3, 7, 11, â¦ until any letter in "p" â¦ "s" is encountered.  E. 3, 7, 11, â¦ until any letter other than "p" â¦ "s" is encountered.
Correct Answer:  D
Explanation:
Since the search is for a four-letter sequence, the idea in this algorithm is that if you examine every fourth slot, youâll find a letter in the required sequence very quickly. When you find one of these letters, you can then examine adjacent slots to check if you have the required sequence. This method will, on average, result in fewer comparisons than the strictly sequential search algorithm in choice A. Choice B is wrong. Question: 206
6.  The  partition  method for quicksort partitions a list as follows.  (i) A pivot element is selected from the array.   (ii) The elements of the list are rearranged such that all elements to the left of the pivot are less than or equal to it; all elements to the right of the pivot are greater than or equal to it.  Partitioning the array requires which of the following?
A. A recursive algorithm  B. A temporary array  C. An external file for the array  D. A swap algorithm for interchanging array elements  E. A merge method for merging two sorted lists
Correct Answer:  D
Explanation:

Question: 207

Question: 210
3.  Consider a binary search algorithm to search an ordered list of numbers. Which of the following choices is closest to the maximum number of times that such an algorithm will execute its main comparison loop when searching a list of 1 million numbers?
A. 6  B. 20  C. 100  D. 120  E. 1000
Correct Answer:  B
Explanation:
1 million = 10<sup>6</sup> = (10<sup>3</sup>)<sup>2</sup> â (2<sup>10</sup>)<sup>2</sup> = 2<sup>20</sup>. Thus, there will be on the order of 20 comparisons.
#########################################################
Question: 211
4.  Consider these three tasks.  I. A sequential search of an array of <i>n</i> names  II. A binary search of an array of <i>n</i> names in alphabetical order  III. An insertion sort into alphabetical order of an array of <i>n</i> names that are initially in random order  For large <i>n</i>, which of the following lists these tasks in order (from least to greatest) of their average case run times?
A. II I III  B. I II III  C. II III I  D. III I II  E. III II I
Correct Answer:  A
Explanation:
A binary search, on average, has a smaller run time than a sequential search. All of the sorting algorithms have greater run times than a sequential search. This is because a sequential search looks at each element once. A sorting algorithm, however, processes <i>other</i> elements in the array for each element it looks at.
#########################################################
Question: 212
5.  Suppose the game is programmed so that the computer uses a binary search strategy for making its guesses. What is the maximum number of guesses the computer could make before guessing the userâs number?
A. 50  B. 25  C. 10  D. 7  E. 6
Correct Answer:  D
Explanation:
The computer should find the number in no more than seven tries. This is because the guessing interval is halved on each successive try:  <div class="table-responsive"><table class="table table-bordered"><tr><td> (1) </td><td>  100 Ã· 2 = 50 numbers left to try </td></tr><tr><td> (2) </td><td> 50 Ã· 2 = 25 numbers left to try </td></tr><tr><td> (3) </td><td> 25 Ã· 2 = 13 numbers left to try </td></tr><tr><td> (4) </td><td> 13 Ã· 2 = 7 numbers left to try </td></tr><tr><td> (5) </td><td> 7 Ã· 2 = 4 numbers left to try </td></tr><tr><td> (6) </td><td> 4 Ã· 2 = 2 numbers left to try </td></tr><tr><td> (7) </td><td> 2 Ã· 2 = 1 number left to try </td></tr></table>  Seven iterations of the loop leaves just 1 number left to try! Donât forget the shortcut. The algorithm is a binary search of 100 possible elements. Rounding 100 up to the next power of 2 gives 128 = 2<sup>7</sup>. The exponent, 7, is the number of guesses in the worst case.
#########################################################
Question: 213
6.  Suppose the computer used a <i>sequential search</i> strategy for guessing the userâs number. What is the maximum number of guesses the computer could make before guessing the userâs number?
A. 100  B. 99  C. 50  D. 25  E. 10
Correct Answer:  B
Explanation:
The maximum number of guesses is 99. A sequential search means that the computer starts at the first possible numberânamely, 1âand tries each successive number until it gets to 99. If the userâs number is 100, the computer will know that when it tests 99.
#########################################################
Question: 214
7.  Using a sequential search strategy, how many guesses <i>on average</i> would the computer need to guess the number?
A. 100  B. Between 51 and 99  C. 50  D. 25  E. Fewer than 25
Correct Answer:  C
Explanation:
On average the computer will make 50 guesses. The user is equally likely to pick any number between 1 and 100. Half the time it will be less than 50; half the time, greater than 50. So on the average, the distance of the number from 1 is 50.

Question: 215
1.  Consider the following two methods in the same class.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/qno01_01.png"/>  If the current state of  <span class="text-monospace">mat</span> is <pre>        1 2 3 4 <br/>        5 6 7 8 </pre> which matrix will result from the method call  <span class="text-monospace">changeMatrix(mat);</span> ?
A. <pre>1 2 3 4<br/>5 6 7 8 </pre>  B. <pre>2 3 4 1<br/>6 7 8 5 </pre>  C. <pre>4 1 2 3<br/>8 5 6 7 </pre>  D. <pre>3 1 2 3<br/>7 5 6 7 </pre>  E. <pre>2 3 4 2<br/>6 7 8 6 </pre>
Correct Answer:  E
Explanation:
Answer: E   The <span class="text-monospace">changeArray</span> method shifts the elements of its array parameter (except for <span class="text-monospace">a[0]</span>, which gets overwritten) one slot to the left. Note that <span class="text-monospace">mat[0]</span>, <span class="text-monospace">mat[1]</span>, . . ., <span class="text-monospace">mat[mat.length-1]</span> are the row arrays of <span class="text-monospace">mat</span>.

Question: 216
2.  The Richter scale is used to measure the strength of an earthquake. A value on the scale is a real number between 0 and 10; and each step in the scaleâfor example from 5.0 to 6.0ârepresents a tenfold increase in the strength of the earthquake.  Consider the following class, written by a student, whose intent is to describe the effects of an earthquake.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/qno02_01.png"/>  Consider the following segment of a client program.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/brn_0002_mod.png"/>  If theÂ Richter magnitudeÂ is 4.0, what will be output?
A. <span class="text-monospace">Earth shakes. No destruction.</span>  B. <span class="text-monospace">Poorly-constructed buildings collapse.</span>  C. <span class="text-monospace">Barely felt by people.</span>  D. <span class="text-monospace">Earth shakes. No destruction.Barely felt by people.</span>  E. An error message will be output.
Correct Answer:  C
Explanation:
Answer: C   The intent of the programmer is to set <span class="text-monospace">str</span> to  <span class="text-monospace">Earth shakes. No destruction.</span>  However, because <span class="text-monospace">else</span> is not used, each of the <span class="text-monospace">if</span> statements will be executed, and <span class="text-monospace">str</span> will be set twice, once when it passes the <span class="text-monospace">if (richter &gt;= 3.0)</span> test and again when it passes the <span class="text-monospace">if (richter &gt;= 0)</span> test. The programmer can avoid this either by using a sequence of <span class="text-monospace">else if</span> tests, thus excluding all other tests when one is found to be true, or by returning the appropriate string (with a <span class="text-monospace">return</span> statement) as soon as a test is true.

Question: 217
3.  Suppose  <span class="text-monospace">x</span>,  <span class="text-monospace">y</span>, and  <span class="text-monospace">z</span> are variables of type  <span class="text-monospace">int</span>. Consider the following boolean conditions.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/3.1.png"/>  Which of these expressions is true for all values of <span class="text-monospace">z</span><i>,</i> given that <span class="text-monospace">x</span> and <span class="text-monospace">y</span> have the same value?
A. I only  B. II only  C. III only  D. I and II only  E. II and III only
Correct Answer:  E
Explanation:
Answer: E   For expression I to be true, each of the three tests must be true. Because the values of <span class="text-monospace">(y == z)</span> and <span class="text-monospace">(x == z)</span> are unknown, the truth value of expression I is unknown. Expression II is true if <span class="text-monospace">(x == y)</span> is true: Since <span class="text-monospace">&amp;&amp;</span> (and) has higher precedence than <span class="text-monospace">||</span> (or), you can think of expression II as being <span class="text-monospace">(x == y)</span> OR <i>p</i>, where <i>p</i> is the truth value of <span class="text-monospace">(y == z) &amp;&amp; (x == z)</span>. Given that <span class="text-monospace">(x == y)</span> is true, true OR <i>p</i> must be true, irrespective of whether <i>p</i> is true or false. Expression III is true, since <span class="text-monospace">x - y</span> equals 0, and 0 multiplied by any number of factors equals 0.

Question: 219
5.  Suppose that, of the three classes shown in the diagram, only the  <span class="text-monospace">LibraryItem</span> class has a method called  <span class="text-monospace">getPrice</span> defined in it, whose specification is as follows.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/brn_0004_1_mod.png"> </img>  Now consider the following declaration that appears in a client program.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/brn_0004_2_mod.png"/>   Assume that  <span class="text-monospace">libraryList</span> is initialized with  <span class="text-monospace">LibraryItem</span> objects. Consider the following code segment that computes the total cost of all items stored in  <span class="text-monospace">libraryList</span>.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/brn_0004_mod2.png"/>   The use of  <span class="text-monospace">getPrice</span> in this code segment is an example of
A. an inherited method.  B. an overridden method.  C. polymorphism.  D. an overloaded method.  E. a mutator method.
Correct Answer:  A
Explanation:
Answer: A   Because the <span class="text-monospace">CD</span> and <span class="text-monospace">Book</span> classes are subclasses of <span class="text-monospace">LibraryItem</span>, each inherits <span class="text-monospace">getPrice</span> and can call it in a client class. Each of the other choices has a specific function, none of which is illustrated in the code segment. An overridden method is redefined in a subclass. (This is not true here, because you are given that <span class="text-monospace">getPrice</span> is defined only in the superclass.) Polymorphism operates only when methods are overridden: At run time, the actual subclass instance is bound to the correct version of the method. An overloaded method has the same name as another method in the class or subclass but a difference signature. A mutator method is one that changes the state of an object. The <span class="text-monospace">getPrice</span> method is an <span class="text-monospace">accessor</span>.

Question: 221
7.  A charity organization has a large list of donor records, sorted alphabetically by name. Each record contains the amount of money donated in the current year. Which of the following represents an algorithm that will locate the top seven donors for the current year?
A. Seven passes through the outer loop of an insertion sort  B. Seven passes through the outer loop of a selection sort  C. Seven recursive calls to mergesort  D. Seven passes through the loop of a binary search  E. Accessing the last seven entries in the list
Correct Answer:  B
Explanation:
Answer: B    After seven passes of a selection sort, if you are sorting donors from largest to smallest amounts of money, the donors with the seven largest amounts will be in their final sorted position. Choice A doesn’t work because after seven passes through an insertion sort loop, the first seven elements will be sorted with respect to each other, but not in their <i>final</i> position. Choice C is completely wrong: Mergesort does not sort the elements into their final position until the final merging of elements. Choice D does not make sense: A binary search is meaningless if the array is not sorted by dollar amounts! Choice E will locate the seven donors whose names are at the end of the alphabetical list. They are not necessarily the people who donated the most money.

Question: 230
6.  What will be output for  <span class="text-monospace">str1</span> by a call to  <span class="text-monospace">mystery</span>?
A. <span class="text-monospace">dogcatcowbird</span>  B. <span class="text-monospace">ogatowird</span>  C. <span class="text-monospace">oaoi</span>  D. <span class="text-monospace">dccb</span>  E. <span class="text-monospace">og</span>

Answer: B   The <span class="text-monospace">substring</span> method, when used with just one parameter, returns the substring of the calling string that starts at the parameter position and extends to the end of the string. Thus, <span class="text-monospace">"dog".substring(1)</span> will return <span class="text-monospace">og</span>. The enhanced <span class="text-monospace">for</span> loop in method <span class="text-monospace">mystery</span> cycles through each string in <span class="text-monospace">list</span> and appends the relevant substring of the current element to <span class="text-monospace">str1</span>: <span class="text-monospace">og</span> + <span class="text-monospace">at</span> + <span class="text-monospace">ow</span> + <span class="text-monospace">ird</span>, resulting in choice B.

Question: 231

Correct Answer:  A
Explanation:
Answer: A   When the <span class="text-monospace">substring</span> method is used with two parameters, the first parameter is where the substring starts, and the second parameter is the position one place to the right of where the substring ends. <span class="text-monospace">"bird".substring(1, 2)</span> will return <span class="text-monospace">i</span>, for example. The enhanced for loop in method <span class="text-monospace">mystery</span> thus appends to <span class="text-monospace">str2</span> a single-character string for each element in <span class="text-monospace">list</span>: <span class="text-monospace">o</span> + <span class="text-monospace">a</span> + <span class="text-monospace">o</span> + <span class="text-monospace">i</span>, resulting in choice A.

Question: 238
4.  In the following code segment, you may assume that  <span class="text-monospace">a</span>,  <span class="text-monospace">b</span>, and  <span class="text-monospace">n</span> are all type  <span class="text-monospace">int</span>.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/brn_0020_mod.png"/>  What will happen if  <span class="text-monospace">a == b</span> is true?
A. <span class="text-monospace">/*  <i>statement 2</i>  */</span> will be executed, followed by  <span class="text-monospace"><i>/* statement 3 */</i></span> .  B. <span class="text-monospace">/*  <i>statement 1</i>  */</span> will be executed, followed by <span class="text-monospace"> <i>/* statement 3 */</i> </span>.  C. Neither <span class="text-monospace">/*  <i>statement 1</i>  */</span> nor  <span class="text-monospace">/*  <i>statement 2</i>  */</span> will be executed. Execution will pass to  <span class="text-monospace">/*  <i>statement 3</i>  */</span>.  D. A compile-time error will occur.  E. An exception will be thrown.
Correct Answer:  A
Explanation:
Answer: A   If <span class="text-monospace">a == b</span> is true, then <span class="text-monospace">a != b</span> is false, and the entire compound <span class="text-monospace">if</span> test will be false, leading to the evaluation of <span class="text-monospace">/*  <i>statement 2</i>  */</span>. Short-circuiting will occur as soon as <span class="text-monospace">a != b</span> is evaluated. This means that <span class="text-monospace">n / (a - b) &gt; 90</span> will never be evaluated. Notice that <span class="text-monospace">n / (a - b)</span> represents division by 0, so if the second piece of the test <i>were</i> evaluated, it would cause an <span class="text-monospace">ArithmeticException</span> to be thrown. If the test executes without error, <span class="text-monospace"><i> /* statement 3 */ </i></span> will always be executed, because it is outside the <span class="text-monospace">if...else</span> statement.

Question: 239
5.  Consider the methodÂ  <span class="text-monospace">printSomething</span>, which prints a piece of its matrix parameter,  <span class="text-monospace">mat</span>.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/qno25_01.png"/>  What will be output from a call to  <span class="text-monospace">printSomething(mat)</span> if  <span class="text-monospace">mat</span> is as shown below?  1 2 3 4<br/> 5 6 7 8<br/> 9 0 1 2<br/> 3 4 5 6
A. <pre>6 8 4 6 </pre>  B. <pre>2 4 0 2 </pre>  C. <pre>5 7 3 5 </pre>  D. <pre>5 3 7 5 </pre>  E. <pre>6 4 8 6 </pre>
Correct Answer:  A
Explanation:
Answer: A   The algorithm traverses the matrix starting with the second row ( <span class="text-monospace">i=1</span>) and second column ( <span class="text-monospace">j=1</span>). The expressions <span class="text-monospace">i+=2</span> and <span class="text-monospace">j+=2</span> cause every other row and column to be skipped. Thus, the second and fourth elements in the second and fourth rows of the matrix will be printed.

Question: 240
6.  Which represents a correct  <span class="text-monospace">/*  <i>implementation</i>  */</span> for the  <span class="text-monospace">increment</span> method?  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/brn_0022_6_mod.png"> </img>

Correct Answer:  D
Explanation:
Answer: D   Suppose the <span class="text-monospace">NumberDisplay</span> represents hours on a 24-hour digital clock. The roll over limit will be 24, and the values will range from 0 to 23 inclusive. Segment III achieves the correct result in a tricky way. Suppose <span class="text-monospace">value</span> is 9. Then <span class="text-monospace">value</span> = (10) % 24 = 10, which was required. Suppose <span class="text-monospace">value</span> is 23. Then <span class="text-monospace">value</span> = (24) % 24 = 0, which is correct.

Question: 241
7.  A digital clock contains two  <span class="text-monospace">NumberDisplay</span> objects, for minutes and hours. Which of the following is the most suitable set of  declarations?
A. <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/brn_0022_1_mod.png"> </img>  B. <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/brn_0022_2_mod.png"/>   C. <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/brn_0022_3_mod.jpg"/>   D. <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/brn_0022_4_mod.png"/>   E. <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/brn_0022_5_mod.png"/>
Correct Answer:  D
Explanation:
Answer: D   The relationship between a <span class="text-monospace">DigitalClock</span> and <span class="text-monospace">NumberDisplay</span> is a <i>has-a</i> relationship: The <span class="text-monospace">DigitalClock </span> <i>has-a </i> <span class="text-monospace">NumberDisplay</span> for hours, and it <i>has-a </i> <span class="text-monospace">NumberDisplay</span> for minutes. There is no inheritance in this relationship, so all of the choices that use "extends" in their class headers are wrong (choices A, B, and C). Choice E is wrong because <span class="text-monospace">hours</span> and <span class="text-monospace">minutes</span> should be of type <span class="text-monospace">NumberDisplay</span>.

Question: 243
9.  Refer to the static method  <span class="text-monospace">removeValue</span>.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/comp_prin_2q.png"/>  Which represents an  <span class="text-monospace">/*  <i>implementation</i>  */</span> of  <span class="text-monospace">removeValue</span> that achieves the postcondition?  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/brn_0024_mod.png"/> <pre></pre>
A. I only  B. II only  C. III only  D. I and III only  E. I, II, and III
Correct Answer:  C
Explanation:
Answer: C   Segment I will not work whenever there are consecutive occurrences of <span class="text-monospace">value</span>. This is because removal of an element from <span class="text-monospace">list</span> causes the elements to the right of it to be shifted to the left to fill the "hole." The index <span class="text-monospace">i</span>, however, moves one slot to the right. For example, if <span class="text-monospace">list</span> contains 1, 6, 6, 9, and 6 is the value to be removed, <span class="text-monospace">list</span> will end up with 1, 6, 9. (The first occurrence of 6 will be removed. The second occurrence will be passed over.) Segment III, a correct algorithm, works because the index shifts right only if an element was not equal to <span class="text-monospace">value</span>. You should reject segment II as soon as you see it. An enhanced <span class="text-monospace">for</span> loop should not be used to remove elements from a list.

2.  A client class has an  <span class="text-monospace">ArrayList&lt;Bird&gt; birds</span> that is initialized with many different objects that are subclasses of  <span class="text-monospace">Bird</span>. Each subclass has an overridden  <span class="text-monospace">makeNoise</span> method, similar to those shown in the  <span class="text-monospace">Owl</span> and  <span class="text-monospace">Hen</span> classes. What is the effect of executing the following code segment?  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/brn_0026_mod.png"> </img>
A. The unique noise for each particular  <span class="text-monospace">Bird</span> will be output.  B. There will be a compile-time error with a message to the effect that there cannot  be different types in  <span class="text-monospace">ArrayList&lt;Bird&gt;</span>.  C. There will be a compile-time error with a message to the effect that  <span class="text-monospace">Bird b</span> needs to be cast to its actual type.  D. Question: 248
4.  An array of hospital records is sorted by patient ID numbers. Suppose a patient's record must be located given the patient's name only. Which of the following procedures is the most efficient for locating that patient's record?
A. Do a binary search.  B. Do a sequential search.  C. Sort the array into alphabetical order, then do a binary search.  D. Sort the array into alphabetical order, then do a sequential search.  E. Start with the first record and examine every fifth record. If this fails, start with the second record and examine every fourth record. If this fails, start with the third record and examine every third record. Proceed in this way until the record with the given name is found.
Correct Answer:  B
Explanation:
Answer: B   The records are not ordered by name, so the quickest way to find the given record is to start at the first record and proceed sequentially through the records until you find the given name. Eliminate choice A: You can't do a binary search for a given name unless the array is sorted by <i>name</i>. Choices C and D will eventually locate the given record, but it is inefficient to start by sorting the array. Since sorting requires the examination of every record anyway, you may as well omit the sort and start with the sequential search! The fancy algorithm in choice E doesn't save time. It, in fact, examines some records more than once!
#########################################################
Question: 249
5.  Which of the following is (are) false?  <ol style="list-style-type:upper-roman">  A subclass inherits all the constructors of its superclass.   A subclass inherits all the private instance variables of its superclass.   A subclass inherits all the methods of its superclass.  </ol>
A. I only  B. II only  C. III only  D. I and II only  E. I, II, and III
Correct Answer:  E
Explanation:
Answer: E    <p data-uid="">Constructors are never inherited, nor are private instance variables. To access the private data of its superclass, a subclass must use the inherited accessor methods of the superclass. Statement III is false because a subclass does not inherit the private methods of its superclass.

Question: 252
8.  Of the following, which is the most appropriate header in a static client class for a  <span class="text-monospace">nameMatch</span> method that determines whether two  <span class="text-monospace">Employee</span>s have the same name?
A. <span class="text-monospace">public static boolean nameMatch(Employee other)</span>  B. <span class="text-monospace">public static void nameMatch(Employee other)</span>  C. <span class="text-monospace">public static boolean nameMatch(Name other)</span>  D. <span class="text-monospace">public static void nameMatch(Employee emp1, Employee emp2)</span>  E. <span class="text-monospace">public static boolean nameMatch(Employee emp1, Employee emp2)</span>
Correct Answer:  E
Explanation:
Answer: E   This is an objectless client method, so there is no current <span class="text-monospace">Employee</span> object. This means that the method needs two <span class="text-monospace">Employee</span> parameters to compare. You can therefore eliminate choices A, B, and C. Note that the method should return true if the <span class="text-monospace">Employee</span> parameters have the same name, false otherwise. Therefore, the method should have a <span class="text-monospace">boolean</span> return type, and you can eliminate choice D.

Question: 253
9.  The following method is intended to return the index of the "smallest" word in the array <span class="text-monospace">words</span>, namely the word that would appear first in an alphabetized list of the strings in the array.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/brn_0032_mod.png"/>  Which of the following should be used to replace  <span class="text-monospace">/* condition */</span> so that  <span class="text-monospace">findMin</span> works as intended?
A. <span class="text-monospace">words[minPos] &gt; words[index]</span>  B. <span class="text-monospace">words[index] &gt; words[minPos]</span>  C. <span class="text-monospace">words[index].compareTo(words[minPos]) &gt; 0</span>  D. <span class="text-monospace">words[index].compareTo(words[minPos]) &gt;= 0</span>  E. <span class="text-monospace">words[index].compareTo(words[minPos]) &lt; 0</span>
Correct Answer:  E
Explanation:
Answer: E   Eliminate choices A and B: When comparing <span class="text-monospace">String</span> objects, you cannot use simple inequality operators; you <i>must</i> use <span class="text-monospace">compareTo</span>. For the calling object to be <i>less than</i> the parameter object, use the <i>less than</i> 0 test (a good way to remember this!).

Question: 254
10.  Consider the following static method,  <span class="text-monospace">countDiff</span>. Method  <span class="text-monospace">countDiff</span> is intended to count the number of different values in array  <span class="text-monospace">arr</span>. It does not, however, work as intended. (Lines are numbered for reference.)  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/40.1.png"/>  Which of the following changes should be made so that  <span class="text-monospace">countDiff</span> will work as intended?
A. <span class="cambria">Line 8 should be changed to</span> <span class="text-monospace">int count = 0;</span>  B. <span class="cambria">Line 9 should be changed to</span> <span class="text-monospace">for (int i = 0; i &lt; arr.length - 1; i++)</span>  C. <span class="cambria">Line 11 should be changed to</span> <span class="text-monospace">if (arr[i] == arr[i + 1])</span>  D. <span class="cambria">Line 16 should be changed to</span> <span class="text-monospace">return arr.length - count;</span>  E. <span class="cambria">Line 16 should be changed to</span> <span class="text-monospace">return count - arr.length;</span>
Correct Answer:  B
Explanation:
Answer: B   In the given implementation of the method, <span class="text-monospace">count</span> is incremented every time a different value is encountered, which is what was required. The problem in the code is that if line 9 is not changed, when the last index in the array is reached, <span class="text-monospace">arr[i + 1]</span> is out of range and an exception will be thrown ( <span class="text-monospace">ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException</span>). Assuming that line 9 is fixed, each of the other choices will cause an intent error. Choice A will return a count that is off by one. Choice C will increment the count when two adjacent values are the same, which is not what was required. Choice D will give a count of each occurrence of a duplicate value-not required. Choice E will give zero or a negative value, which doesn't make sense.

Question: 260
6.  Refer to the following method.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg70_01.png"/>  What will  <span class="text-monospace">weirdStr</span> contain after the following code is executed?  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/brn_0043_mod.png"/>

The <span class="text-monospace">for</span> loop thus cycles through <span class="text-monospace">"conglomeration,"</span> starting at <span class="text-monospace">"c,"</span> and compares each single character string to <span class="text-monospace">"m."</span> If that character precedes <span class="text-monospace">"m,"</span> a new <span class="text-monospace">String</span> reference <span class="text-monospace">w</span> is created, which consists of the current value of <span class="text-monospace">w</span> concatenated with that character. Notice that every character in the string <span class="text-monospace">"cgleai"</span> precedes <span class="text-monospace">"m"</span> in alphabetical order.

Question: 263
9.  Consider array <span class="text-monospace">arr</span>, which is initialized as follows.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg73_01.png"/>  Which statement about a sequential search or binary search is <i>false</i>?
A. A key of 20 represents a worst case for sequential search.  B. A key of 8 represents a best case for binary search.  C. A key of 0 represents a worst case for sequential search.  D. A key of 20 represents a worst case for binary search.  E. A key of 30 represents a worst case for both sequential and binary searches.
Correct Answer:  C
Explanation:
Answer: C    In a sequential search in a sorted array, a key that is less than the first element will be revealed almost immediately in the search, and so cannot be a worst case. Choice A is true because the search algorithm must search the whole array before 20 is found. Choice B is true because <span class="text-monospace">arr[(0 + 7)/2] = arr[3]</span> will be the first element compared to the key. Choice D is true because a rightmost endpoint is a worst case for binary search, whereas a leftmost endpoint would not be, because the div operation skews to the left. Choice E is true because an element that is to the right of the largest element of the array will need the maximum number of passes through the search algorithms (both binary and sequential) to discover that it’s not in the array.
#########################################################
Question: 264
10.  Which statement about constructors is <i>false</i>?
A. It is legal for the value of a static variable to be changed in a constructor.  B. The constructor in a subclass must use the keyword  <span class="text-monospace">super</span> to initialize the private instance variables from its superclass.  C. A subclass can have a default constructor that differs from the default constructor of its superclass.  D. A subclass has fewer constructors than its superclass.  E. If a subclass does not explicitly provide a constructor and its superclass has justone constructor with a parameter, an error will occur when an attempt is made to createan instance of a subclass object.
Correct Answer:  D
Explanation:
Answer: D   A subclass can have any number of constructors. Each of the other statements is true. For choice A, a static variable stores information for the entire class. For example, it could provide a new serial number each time an object is created. To do this, the variable must be updated in the constructor. For choice B, a subclass cannot directly access the private instance variables of its superclass. It therefore <i>must</i> use <span class="text-monospace">super</span> to invoke the constructor of the superclass to initialize those variables. For choice C, the default constructor of a subclass often initializes new private instance variables that are not in the superclass. For choice E, if there is no constructor in a subclass, code for a superclass default constructor will be provided by the compiler. If the superclass does not have a default constructor, there will be a compile-time error.

Question: 267
3.  Which is a true statement about the methods in  <span class="text-monospace">ClassA</span> and  <span class="text-monospace">ClassB</span>?
A. <span class="text-monospace">ClassB</span> inherits  <span class="text-monospace">method2</span> from  <span class="text-monospace">ClassA</span>.  B. <span class="text-monospace">ClassA</span> inherits  <span class="text-monospace">method2</span> from  <span class="text-monospace">ClassB</span>.  C. <span class="text-monospace">method1</span> is an example of an overloaded method.  D. <span class="text-monospace">method2</span> is an example of an overridden method.  E. <span class="text-monospace">method1</span> is an example of an overridden method.
Correct Answer:  E
Explanation:
Answer: E   An overridden method is an inherited method whose implementation is changed in the subclass (same header, different body). Since <span class="text-monospace">method1</span> fits this description, choice E is true and choice D is false. For choice A, <span class="text-monospace">method2</span> is defined for the first time in <span class="text-monospace">ClassB</span>. Therefore, it is not inherited. For choice B, a superclass <i>never</i> inherits a method from its subclass. For choice C, for <span class="text-monospace">method1</span> to be an overloaded method, it would need a different signature in <span class="text-monospace">ClassB</span>.

Question: 269
5.  Consider the <span class="text-monospace">ElapsedTime</span> constructor that creates an <span class="text-monospace">ElapsedTime</span> object from its <span class="text-monospace">numSecs</span> parameter.  Recall that there are 60 seconds in a minute, and 60 minutes in an hour.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg79_01a.png"> </img>  Which of the following is a correct /* <span class="text-monospace">ElapsedTimeÂ  <i>implementation code</i>  */?</span>  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg79_02.png"/>
A. I only  B. II only  C. III only  D. I and III only  E. I, II, and III
Correct Answer:  C
Explanation:
Answer: C   Implementation III is correct: The number of seconds equals the remainder when <span class="text-monospace">numSecs</span> is divided by 60; the number of minutes equals the quotient when <span class="text-monospace">numSecs</span> is divided by 60; and the number of hours equals the quotient when the number of minutes is divided by 60.  A constructor must assign values to the private instance variables, in a way that satisfies their specifications. Implementation I fails because it doesn’t assign values to <span class="text-monospace">hours</span> and <span class="text-monospace">mins</span>, and also because <span class="text-monospace">secs</span> should be no greater than 59. Implementation II fails on the assignment of <span class="text-monospace">secs</span>. For example, if <span class="text-monospace">numSecs</span> is 67, <span class="text-monospace">hours</span> is 0, <span class="text-monospace">mins</span> is 1, but <span class="text-monospace">secs</span> is not equal to 67 - (0 + 1).

Correct Answer:  C
Explanation:
Answer: C   Denote <span class="text-monospace">mystery(6)</span> as <i>m</i>(6). The following diagram follows <i>m</i>(6) to its base case (shaded), which returns the value 2.  <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/t2_s1_018.png"/>  Going up the left-hand side of the tree, you can see the pattern:  <span class="text-monospace"><i>m</i>(3) = 2 + 2 = 4<br/> <i>m</i>(4) = 4 + 2 = 6<br/> <i>m</i>(5) = 6 + 4 = 1<span class="cambria">0</span><br/> <i>m</i>(6) = 1<span class="cambria">0</span> + 6 = 16</span>

A <span class="text-monospace">ConcurrentModificationException</span> will be thrown.  C. A  <span class="text-monospace">NullPointerException</span> will be thrown.  D. Question: 279
5.  An array of 10,000  <span class="text-monospace">Student</span> objects,  <span class="text-monospace">arr[0]</span>,  <span class="text-monospace">arr[1]</span>, . . .,  <span class="text-monospace">arr[9999]</span> is to be searched for a particular  <span class="text-monospace">Student</span> whose ID number only is known. In order to do a binary search, which of the following is a necessary precondition?
A. The array is sorted by ID number.  B. The array is in alphabetical order by name.  C. The array is sorted by ID number and alphabetically by name.  D. The ID number key is in the array.  E. No two students in the array have the same name.
Correct Answer:  A
Explanation:
Answer: A    For this search, the key being searched for is an ID number. Therefore, the array must be sorted by ID number. Suppose the key being searched for was a student's name. Then the array would need to be sorted by name to use a binary search.

Question: 280
6.  Given that all sorting algorithms strive to be efficient in terms of time and memory usage, which of the following is the biggest disadvantage of merge sort?
A. The algorithm uses recursion.  B. The algorithm uses a divide-and-conquer algorithm, which is inefficient.  C. It requires a temporary array.  D. In its worst case it is very inefficient.  E. The merge method is inefficient.
Correct Answer:  C
Explanation:
Answer: C    A temporary array in a recursive method slows it down because the array is created for each recursive call. The other choices are incorrect. For choice A, without recursion merge sort would lose its elegance. For choice B, divide-and-conquer algorithms are some of the <i>most</i> efficient algorithms. For choice D, there is not much difference in the efficiency for best, average, and worst cases. For choice E, because of the divide-and-conquer aspect of merge sort, it is more efficient than selection sort or insertion sort, for example.

Question: 287
3.  Which of the following activities, performed by the programmer, would be an example of procedural abstraction?
A. Deciding to use methods  <span class="text-monospace">getCourses</span> and  <span class="text-monospace">getPeriods</span> to set up a  <span class="text-monospace">Schedule</span> for a  <span class="text-monospace">Teacher</span>.  B. Combining the data fields  <span class="text-monospace">name</span> and  <span class="text-monospace">schedule</span> with methods needed in a  <span class="text-monospace">Teacher</span> class.  C. Using private methods in the  <span class="text-monospace">Teacher</span> class to restrict access to some information.  D. Implementing the controller class  <span class="text-monospace">ScheduleManager</span> first, followed by the lower-level subsidiary classes.  E. Writing a <span class="text-monospace">Display</span> class first so that classes like  <span class="text-monospace">Teacher</span> and  <span class="text-monospace">Course</span> can be tested early in the development process.
Correct Answer:  A
Explanation:
Answer: A   Procedural abstraction is the process of coming up with separate methods that will encapsulate each behavior in a class. Each of the other choices is incorrect. Choice B is an example of <i>encapsulation</i>, the combining of data fields and methods in a class. Choice C is an example of <i>information hiding</i>, using <span class="text-monospace">private</span> to restrict access. Choice D is an example of <i>top-down development</i>, implementing the main classes first, the lower-level classes later. Choice E is not an example of anything in particular. While it may be a good idea, it’s not an example of procedural abstraction.

Question: 288
4.  Consider the class <span class="text-monospace">WordPrinter</span> below, which has a recursive method  <span class="text-monospace">printSomething</span>.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/comp_prin_2ad.png"/>  What will be output by the following method call?  <span class="text-monospace">Â Â Â Â Â printSomething(245);</span>
A. <span class="text-monospace">five four two</span>  B. <span class="text-monospace">two hundred forty five</span>  C. <span class="text-monospace">two four five</span>  D. <span class="text-monospace">two five four</span>  E. <span class="text-monospace">four two five</span>
Correct Answer:  C
Explanation:
Answer: C   Each time a recursive call is made to <span class="text-monospace">printSomething</span>, execution goes back to the start of a new method call, but must remember to execute the pending statements for each call. <span class="text-monospace">printSomething(245)</span> calls <span class="text-monospace">printSomething(24)</span> and stacks <span class="text-monospace">System.out.print(" ")</span> and <span class="text-monospace">printDigit(5)</span>. Then <span class="text-monospace">printSomething(24)</span> calls <span class="text-monospace">printSomething(2)</span> and stacks <span class="text-monospace">System.out.print(" ")</span> and <span class="text-monospace">printDigit(4)</span>. The stack of pending calls can be pictured as follows: <div> <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/t2_s1_034.png"/>   Finally, <span class="text-monospace">printSomething(2)</span> is a base case, so <span class="text-monospace">two</span> is printed. Now the stack is popped from the top, producing the output <span class="text-monospace">two four five</span>.

Question: 289
5.  Which of the following preconditions suggests using an insertion sort, rather than some other sorting algorithm?
A. The elements are already sorted.  B. The elements are sorted in reverse sorted order.  C. The elements are in random order.  D. The elements are integers.  E. Best case, average case, and worst case are the same.
Correct Answer:  A
Explanation:
Answer: A    Recall that in insertion sort, the first element, <span class="text-monospace">a[0]</span>, can be thought of as being sorted with respect to itself. Think of the array as consisting of two lists, a sorted list followed by an unsorted list. Each element in the unsorted list is moved into the sorted part by finding its insertion point and then shifting elements to create a slot. If the array is already sorted, then the insertion point for any element will be its current position. There will be no more than one test for each element and no shifting of elements to create a slot-the best case for insertion sort.  The worst case is the array sorted in reverse order, choice B. This is because the insertion point will always be at the front of the array, causing the maximum possible number of tests and data moves. Choice C represents an average case, where one could expect a large number of tests and data moves about half the time. Choice D is completely wrong: The type of elements in the array does not affect the efficiency of the sorting algorithm.
#########################################################
Question: 290
6.  Consider a matrix with the declaration  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg104_01.png"/>  where  <span class="text-monospace">nRows</span> and  <span class="text-monospace">nCols</span> are positive integers.  The following code segment is intended to replace all single-character strings inthe matrix with the empty string.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg104_02.png"/>  Which replacements for  <span class="text-monospace">/* missing code 1 */</span> and  <span class="text-monospace">/* missing code 2 */</span>, respectively, will cause the segment to work as intended?  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/comp_prin_2ae.png"/>
A. I only  B. II only  C. III only  D. I and II only  E. I and III only
Correct Answer:  C
Explanation:
Answer: C   The point of this question is that you should know that the number of rows in matrix <span class="text-monospace">m</span> is given by <span class="text-monospace">m.length</span> and the number of columns is <span class="text-monospace">m[r].length</span>, where <span class="text-monospace">m[r]</span> is row <span class="text-monospace">r</span> in the matrix. <span class="text-monospace">/* missing code 1 */</span> traverses the rows, so you need the test <span class="text-monospace">r&lt;strMat.length</span>, while <span class="text-monospace">/* missing code 2 */</span> traverses the columns, so you need the test <span class="text-monospace">c&lt;strMat[r].length</span>. Only segment III uses the correct test in each piece of missing code.

Example 1:  <div> <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/t2_s1_040a.png"/>    Example 2:  <div> <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/t2_s1_040b.png"/>   The following implementation of the perfect shuffle method does not work as intended.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg111_01.png"/>  Which of the following is a problem with the given implementation of the perfect shufflemethod? <ol style="list-style-type:upper-roman">  Executing  <span class="text-monospace">perfectShuffle</span> may cause an  <span class="text-monospace">ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException</span>. Question: 295
1.  A student's test score can be any real number between 0 and 100. The intent of thefollowing class is to print a student's score as a letter grade.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg130_01.png"/>  Consider the following segment of a client program.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/comp_prin_3a.png"/>  If  <span class="text-monospace">testScore</span> is 75.0, what will be output?
A. <span class="text-monospace">Average score.<br/>Barely passing.<br/>Failing score.</span>  B. <span class="text-monospace">Average score.<br/>Barely passing.</span>  C. <span class="text-monospace">Average score.</span>  D. <span class="text-monospace">Congratulations!<br/>Good job.<br/>Average score.</span>  E. An error message will be output.

Explanation:

The programmer can avoid this either by using a sequence of <span class="text-monospace">else if</span> tests, thus excluding all other tests when one is found to be true, or by returningthe appropriate string (with a <span class="text-monospace">return</span> statement) as soon as a test is true.

Question: 298
4.  Consider the following classes, where  <span class="text-monospace">Clown</span> and  <span class="text-monospace">Acrobat</span> are subclasses of  <span class="text-monospace">CircusPerformer</span>. <div>  <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/t3_s1_004.png"> </img>    Which of the following is a <i>true</i> statement about the classes shown?
A. Each of the classes- <span class="text-monospace">CircusPerformer</span>,  <span class="text-monospace">Clown</span>, and  <span class="text-monospace">Acrobat</span>-can have a method  <span class="text-monospace">doTrick</span> that has different code.  B. Both  <span class="text-monospace">Clown</span> and  <span class="text-monospace">Acrobat</span> inherit the constructors in  <span class="text-monospace">CircusPerformer</span>.  C. If  <span class="text-monospace">CircusPerformer</span> has a private instance variable  <span class="text-monospace">routine</span>, both  <span class="text-monospace">Clown</span> and  <span class="text-monospace">Acrobat</span> can directly access it.  D. If  <span class="text-monospace">CircusPerformer</span> has a private method  <span class="text-monospace">tumble</span>, both  <span class="text-monospace">Clown</span> and  <span class="text-monospace">Acrobat</span> can access it.  E. If  <span class="text-monospace">Clown</span> has a private instance variable  <span class="text-monospace">jokes</span>,  <span class="text-monospace">CircusPerformer</span> can access it.
Correct Answer:  A
Explanation:
Answer: A    Statement A is true because the <span class="text-monospace">doTrick</span> method can be overridden in each of its subclasses. Choice B is false because constructors are never inherited. If a subclass has no constructor, the default constructor for the superclass is generated. If the superclass does not have a default constructor, a compile-time error will occur. Choice C is false because the subclasses cannot directly access private instance variables of the superclass. (What they can do is use accessor methods of the superclass.) Choice D is false because a private method in any class can only be accessed in the code of that class. Choice E is false because a superclass cannot access the private instance variables of its subclasses.

Question: 302
8.  Consider the following guessing game:  Consider the problem of writing a game in which a user thinks of an integer from 1 to 1,000 inclusive and the computer tries to guess that number. Each time the computer makes a guess, the user makes one of three responses:   "lower" (i.e., the number is lower than the computer's guess)  "higher" (i.e., the number is higher than the computer's guess)  "you got it in &lt; <i>however many</i> &gt; tries!"    Suppose the game is programmed so that the computer uses a binary search strategyfor making its guesses. What is the maximum number of guesses the computer could makebefore guessing the user's number?
A. 9  B. 10  C. 100  D. 500  E. 1,000
Correct Answer:  B
Explanation:
Answer: B   The computer should find the number in no more than 10 tries. This is because the guessing interval is halved on each successive try:  <span class="text-monospace">(1) 1,<span class="cambria">000</span> Ã· 2 = 5<span class="cambria">00</span> numbers left to try<br/> (2)  5<span class="cambria">00</span> Ã· 2 = 25<span class="cambria">0</span> numbers left to try<br/> (3)  25<span class="cambria">0</span> Ã· 2 = 125   numbers left to try<br/> (4)  125 Ã· 2 =  63  numbers left to try (at most)<br/> (5)  63 Ã· 2 =  32  numbers left to try (at most)<br/> (6)  32 Ã· 2 =  16  numbers left to try<br/> (7)  16 Ã· 2 =  8  numbers left to try<br/> (8)   8 Ã· 2 =  4  numbers left to try<br/> (9)   4 Ã· 2 =  2  numbers left to try<br/> (1<span class="cambria">0</span>)  2 Ã· 2 =  1   number left to try<br/></span>  Ten iterations of the loop leaves just 1 number left to try. Alternatively, round 1,000 to the nearest higher power of 2: 1,000 ≃ 1,024 = 2<sup>10</sup>. The maximum number of guesses (worst case) equals the exponent, 10.
#########################################################
Question: 303
9.  Consider the following guessing game:  Consider the problem of writing a game in which a user thinks of an integer from 1 to 1,000 inclusive and the computer tries to guess that number. Each time the computer makes a guess, the user makes one of three responses:   "lower" (i.e., the number is lower than the computer's guess)  "higher" (i.e., the number is higher than the computer's guess)  "you got it in &lt; <i>however many</i> &gt; tries!"    Suppose the computer starts by guessing a random integer between 1 and 1,000, andthen uses a <i>sequential search</i> strategy to find the user's number. What is the maximum number of guesses the computercould make before guessing the user's number?
A. 50  B. 250  C. 500  D. 999  E. 1,000
Correct Answer:  D
Explanation:
Answer: D   The maximum number of guesses is 999. Suppose the user's number is 1,000 and the computer's first guess happens to be 1. In a sequential search, the computer will try each successive number until it gets to 999. Therefore, in this worst case, the computer will take 999 guesses to reach the user's number. If 999 isn’t the user’s number, then the user’s number must be 1000.
#########################################################
Question: 304
10.  Consider this hierarchy of classes: <div> <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/comp_prin_3c.png"/>   The  <span class="text-monospace">Entree</span> class has a method  <span class="text-monospace">printRecipe</span> with the following header.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg138_01.png"/>  The method is overridden in each of the subclasses shown above. A client class  <span class="text-monospace">RecipeBook</span> has a private instance variable  <span class="text-monospace">allRecipes</span> declared as follows.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg138_02.png"/>  Assuming that  <span class="text-monospace">allRecipes</span> is correctly initialized, the following piece of code is now executed to print a recipe for each subclass dish.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg138_03.png"/>  Which concept is illustrated by this code?
A. Overloaded methods  B. Polymorphism  C. Information hiding  D. Procedural abstraction  E. Encapsulation
Correct Answer:  B
Explanation:
Answer: B   Using polymorphism, the correct <span class="text-monospace">printRecipe</span> method for a given subclass will be selected at run time. Note that the <span class="text-monospace">printRecipe</span> method must be overridden in each of the <span class="text-monospace">Entree</span> subclasses for this to happen correctly. Recall that:    overloaded methods are two or more methods in the same class that have the same name but different parameter lists.    information hiding is the use of <span class="text-monospace">private</span> to restrict access.    procedural abstraction is using separate methods to encapsulate each task in a class.   encapsulation is the combining of data fields and methods in a class.

Question: 305
1.  Which is a <i>false</i> statement about static methods?
A. A static method can use a static variable in its implementation code.  B. If a class is such that it doesn't make sense to ever create an object of the class, then all methods of that class should be static.  C. All methods in a class that has a main method and no private data fields should be static.  D. A static method should not be invoked by an object of a class.  E. Accessor methods in an object class may be static, depending on the value that's being accessed.
Correct Answer:  E
Explanation:
Answer: E    It doesn't make sense to make an accessor static, because an object will then not be able to invoke that method! Note that a static method belongs to the whole class, not an instance of it. It therefore should be invoked in a client class by using the name of the class that defines the method. For example, for a <span class="text-monospace">BankAccount</span> class one might have <span class="text-monospace">BankAccount.getInterestRate().</span> If a specific class object is used to invoke the method (instead of the class name), a good compiler will give a warning that this usage is discouraged.

Question: 306
2.  A programmer needs to produce a random  <span class="text-monospace">int</span> <i>n</i> in the range 20 â¤ <i>n</i> â¤ 30. A statement that does this correctly is
A. <span class="text-monospace">int n = 10*Math.random() + 20;</span>  B. <span class="text-monospace">int n = 11*Math.random() + 20;</span>  C. <span class="text-monospace">int n = (int) (Math.random()) + 20;</span>  D. <span class="text-monospace">int n = (int) (Math.random() * 11) + 20;</span>  E. <span class="text-monospace">int n = (int) (Math.random() * 10) + 20;</span>
Correct Answer:  D
Explanation:
Answer: D    What you need is to produce a random integer in the range 0 to 10, inclusive, and then shift the range by 20. The expression   <span class="text-monospace">   (int) (Math.random() * 11)</span>   produces a random integer from 0 to 10, inclusive. (Note that there are 11 possible numbers.) Adding 20 gives the required range.

Question: 307
3.  Consider the following class definitions.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/comp_prin_3r.png"/>  Assuming that both <span class="text-monospace">Flyer</span> and  <span class="text-monospace">Bird</span>  have default constructors, which is (are) valid in a client class? <ol style="list-style-type:upper-roman">   <span class="text-monospace">Flyer f1 = new Bird();</span>     <span class="text-monospace">Bird b = new Sparrow();</span>     <span class="text-monospace">Flyer f2 = new Sparrow();</span>   </ol>
A. I only  B. II only  C. III only  D. I and II only  E. I, II, and III
Correct Answer:  E
Explanation:
Answer: E   All satisfy the <i>is-a</i> test. <span class="text-monospace">Bird</span> <i>is-a</i> <span class="text-monospace">Flyer</span>; <span class="text-monospace">Sparrow</span> <i>is-a</i> <span class="text-monospace">Bird</span>; <span class="text-monospace">Sparrow</span> <i>is-a</i> <span class="text-monospace">Flyer</span>. Note: Because <span class="text-monospace">Sparrow</span> <i>is-a</i> <span class="text-monospace">Bird</span>, it automatically inherits the methods of <span class="text-monospace">Bird</span>, its superclass. Since <span class="text-monospace">Flyer</span> and <span class="text-monospace">Bird</span> have default constructors, when a new <span class="text-monospace">Sparrow</span> is created, the compiler will slot this code into the <span class="text-monospace">Sparrow</span> class:  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg141_02.png"/>  There would be an error if the superclass did not have a default constructor.
#########################################################
Question: 308
4.  Consider the following class definitions.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg142_01.png"/>  Consider the following declarations in a client class.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/comp_prin_3g.png"/>  Which method calls would be legal? <ol style="list-style-type:upper-roman">   <span class="text-monospace">s.fly();</span>     <span class="text-monospace">b.flyLow(s);</span>     <span class="text-monospace">s.flyLow(b);</span>   </ol>
A. I only  B. II only  C. III only  D. II and III only  E. I, II, and III
Correct Answer:  A
Explanation:
Answer: A   Method call I works because <span class="text-monospace">Sparrow</span> inherits all the methods of <span class="text-monospace">Bird</span>. Method call II fails because <span class="text-monospace">Bird</span>, the superclass, does not inherit the methods of <span class="text-monospace">Sparrow</span>, its subclass. Method call III uses a parameter that fails the <i>is-a</i> test: <span class="text-monospace">b</span> is not a <span class="text-monospace">Sparrow</span>, which the parameter requires.
