Question: 309
5.  Which best describes what the <span class="text-monospace">printSomething</span> method below does?  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg143_01.png"/>
A. It prints string  <span class="text-monospace">s</span>.  B. It prints string  <span class="text-monospace">s</span> in reverse order.  C. It prints only the first character of string  <span class="text-monospace">s</span>.  D. It prints only the first two characters of string  <span class="text-monospace">s</span>.  E. It prints only the last character of string  <span class="text-monospace">s</span>.
Correct Answer:  A
Explanation:
Answer: A    Because the recursive call is made at the end of the method, the <span class="text-monospace">System.out.print...</span> statements are executed at the <i>beginning</i> of each method call, causing the letters of the string to be printed out in order. If the two statements in the method were interchanged, so that the recursive call is made at the beginning of the method, then the pending <span class="text-monospace">print...</span> methods would be stacked up, causing the string to be printed in reverse order.
#########################################################
Question: 310
6.  Refer to the following method that finds the largest value in an array.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg144_01.png"/>  Which replacement(s) for  <span class="text-monospace">/* some value */</span> will always result in correct execution of the  <span class="text-monospace">findMax</span> method? <ol style="list-style-type:upper-roman">   <span class="text-monospace">Integer.MIN_VALUE</span>     <span class="text-monospace">Integer.MAX_VALUE</span>     <span class="text-monospace">arr[0]</span>   </ol>
A. I only  B. II only  C. III only  D. I and III only  E. II and III only
Correct Answer:  D
Explanation:
Answer: D    Because the values in <span class="text-monospace">arr</span> cannot be less than <span class="text-monospace">Integer.MIN_VALUE</span>, the test in the <span class="text-monospace">while</span> loop will be true at least once and will lead to the largest element being stored in <span class="text-monospace">max</span>. (If <i>all</i> the elements of the array are <span class="text-monospace">Integer.MIN_VALUE</span>, the code still works.) Similarly, initializing <span class="text-monospace">max</span> to <span class="text-monospace">arr[0]</span>, the first element in the array, ensures that all elements in <span class="text-monospace">arr</span> will be examined and the largest will be found. Choice II, <span class="text-monospace">Integer.MAX_VALUE</span>, fails because the test in the loop will always be false! There is no array element that will be greater than the largest possible integer. The method will (incorrectly) return <span class="text-monospace">Integer.MAX_VALUE</span>.

Question: 311
7.  An opera company has a large list of donor records, sorted alphabetically by name. Each record contains the amount of money donated in the current year. Which of the following represents the most efficient way to find the name of the top donor in the current year?
A. Insertion sort of the records  B. Selection sort of the records  C. Merge sort of the records  D. Binary search of the records  E. Sequential search of the records
Correct Answer:  E
Explanation:
Answer: E    Because the records are not sorted by amount, each record must be examined to find the one with the largest amount. It therefore doesn't make sense to sort the elements, which involves both examination and movement of elements. So you can eliminate choices A, B, and C. Choice D, the binary search, is wrong because a binary search for an amount can only be done if the list is sorted on that key field. The given list of records is sorted by name, not amount.
#########################################################
Question: 312
8.  Refer to the following code segment.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/comp_prin_3d.png"/>  In terms of  <span class="text-monospace">n</span>, how many times will  <span class="text-monospace">process(i)</span> be executed?
A. <span class="text-monospace">n</span> if  <span class="text-monospace">n</span> is even and  <span class="text-monospace">n + 1</span> if  <span class="text-monospace">n</span> is odd  B. <span class="text-monospace">2</span> <span class="text-monospace">n</span> if  <span class="text-monospace">n</span> is even and  <span class="text-monospace">2 n - 1</span> if  <span class="text-monospace">n</span> is odd  C. <span class="text-monospace">n/2</span> if  <span class="text-monospace">n</span> is even and <span class="text-monospace">1</span> +  <span class="text-monospace">n/2</span> if  <span class="text-monospace">n</span> is odd  D. <span class="text-monospace">n % 2</span> if n is even and <span class="text-monospace">1 + n % 2</span> if <span class="text-monospace">n</span> is odd  E. <span class="text-monospace">2<sup>n</sup></span> if  <span class="text-monospace">n</span> is even and <span class="text-monospace">2<sup>n</sup></span> - <span class="text-monospace">1</span> if  <span class="text-monospace">n</span> is odd
Correct Answer:  C
Explanation:
Answer: C   If you consider a small even number like <span class="text-monospace">4</span>, the loop will be executed when <span class="text-monospace">i</span> is <span class="text-monospace">4</span> and <span class="text-monospace">2</span>, twice. This eliminates choices A, B, and E. If <span class="text-monospace">n</span> is <span class="text-monospace">8</span>, the loop is executed when <span class="text-monospace">i</span> is <span class="text-monospace">8</span>, <span class="text-monospace">6</span>, <span class="text-monospace">4</span>, and <span class="text-monospace">2</span>, four times. Since <span class="text-monospace">n % 2</span> is 0 this eliminates choice D. Notice that choice C also works for any odd integer, <span class="text-monospace">7</span> say. The loop will execute when <span class="text-monospace">i</span> is <span class="text-monospace">7</span>, <span class="text-monospace">5</span>, <span class="text-monospace">3</span>, and <span class="text-monospace">1</span>, four times or <span class="text-monospace">7/2 + 1</span>.

Question: 314
10.  Consider the following classes.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg148_01.png"/>  Suppose that the following constructor is added to the <span class="text-monospace">EvenPosInt</span> class.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg148_02.png"/>  Which of the following is a correct  <span class="text-monospace">/* implementation */</span> for the  <span class="text-monospace">getNextEven</span> method? <ol style="list-style-type:upper-roman">  <span class="text-monospace">return value + 2;</span>   <span class="text-monospace">return getValue() + 2;</span>   <span class="text-monospace">return this.getValue() + 2;</span>  </ol>

Question: 315
1.  Consider a  <span class="text-monospace">Date</span> class whose partial representation is shown below.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg149_01.png"/>  Consider the following declarations.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/comp_prin_3h.png"/>  Based on the given information, which of the following statements <i>must</i> be true?
A. The test  <span class="text-monospace">if (d1 == d2)</span> is  <span class="text-monospace">true</span>.  B. The test  <span class="text-monospace">if (d1.equals(d2))</span> will cause a compile-time error.  C. The test  <span class="text-monospace">if (d1.equals(d2))</span> is  <span class="text-monospace">true</span>.  D. The test  <span class="text-monospace">if (d1.compareTo(d2) == 0)</span> is true.  E. The test  <span class="text-monospace">if (d1.compareTo(d2) == 0)</span> will cause a compile-time error.
Correct Answer:  E
Explanation:
Answer: E   To use the <span class="text-monospace">compareTo</span> method without a compiler error, the class should have a <span class="text-monospace">compareTo</span> method defined, which you are told has not been done. Each of the other statements is false: for choice A, when two objects are compared using <span class="text-monospace">==</span>, the test is false if <span class="text-monospace">d1</span> and <span class="text-monospace">d2</span> are not the same reference. Choice B is false because every class inherits the <span class="text-monospace">equals</span> method from the universal superclass <span class="text-monospace">Object</span>. For choice C, the test will return <span class="text-monospace">true</span> only if the <span class="text-monospace">equals</span> method is overridden in class <span class="text-monospace">Date</span> in such a way that two <span class="text-monospace">Date</span> objects are equal if their <span class="text-monospace">month</span>, <span class="text-monospace">day</span>, and <span class="text-monospace">year</span> data fields are equal. Because you don't know whether <span class="text-monospace">equals</span> has been overridden, you can't state that choice C is true. For choice D, the test can't be true if it doesn't compile. Note: An alternative way to have the <span class="text-monospace">compareTo</span> method compile without error is for the <span class="text-monospace">Date</span> class to implement the <span class="text-monospace">Comparable</span> interface. You are not required to know this for the AP exam.

3. Which of the following replacement(s) for <span class="text-monospace">/* implementation code */</span> correctly achieve(s) this goal? <ol style="list-style-type:upper-roman">   <span class="text-monospace">super();</span>     <span class="text-monospace">super(aSpecialty);</span>     <span class="text-monospace">specialty = aSpecialty;</span>   </ol>

Question: 318
4.  Consider the following declarations.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg153_01.png"/>  A client class has an  <span class="text-monospace">ArrayList&lt;Performer&gt; performers</span> that is initialized with many different objects that are subclasses of  <span class="text-monospace">Performer</span>. Each subclass has an overridden  <span class="text-monospace">doRoutine</span> method, similar to those shown in the  <span class="text-monospace">Dancer</span> and  <span class="text-monospace">BalletDancer</span> classes. What is the effect of executing the following code segment?  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg153_02.png"/>
A. The unique routine for each particular  <span class="text-monospace">Performer</span> will be output.  B. The string "<span class="text-monospace">Do something special.</span>" will be printed for each <span class="text-monospace">p</span> in <span class="text-monospace">performers</span>.  C. The string "<span class="text-monospace">Backflip and spin.</span>" will be printed for each <span class="text-monospace">p</span> in <span class="text-monospace">performers</span>.  D. There will be a compile-time error with a message to the effect that there cannotbe different types in  <span class="text-monospace">ArrayList&lt;Performer&gt;</span>.  E. A run-time error will occur.
Correct Answer:  A
Explanation:
Answer: A   The code will work as intended; namely, at run time, the appropriate <span class="text-monospace">doRoutine</span> method will be called, depending on the current instance of <span class="text-monospace">Performer p</span>. This is an example of polymorphism or dynamic binding. Polymorphism occurs when a superclass method has been overridden in the subclass(es).

Question: 319
5.  A class has a two-dimensional squarearray.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/comp_prin_3i.png"/>  The array is initialized to have  <span class="text-monospace">SIZE</span> rows and columns. Consider the following method in the class.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg155_02.png"/>  Which of the following could be the resulting matrix after a call to <span class="text-monospace">fillArray("obtaining")</span>, assuming that the method runs without error? <ol style="list-style-type:upper-roman">  <span class="text-monospace">o b t aÂ </span>  <li class="no-number"><span class="text-monospace">i n i n</span>  <li class="no-number"><span class="text-monospace">g 0 0 0Â </span>  <li class="no-number"><span class="text-monospace">0 0 0 0</span>   <span class="text-monospace">o b tÂ </span>  <li class="no-number"><span class="text-monospace">a i n</span>  <li class="no-number"><span class="text-monospace">Â i n g</span>   <span class="text-monospace">o bÂ </span>  <li class="no-number"><span class="text-monospace">t a</span>  </ol>
A. I only  B. II only  C. III only  D. I and II only  E. I, II, and III
Correct Answer:  E
Explanation:
Answer: E   All are correct, depending on whether <span class="text-monospace">SIZE</span> is 4, 3, or 2. The method fills the two-dimensional square array <span class="text-monospace">strMat</span> with single-character strings obtained with <span class="text-monospace">str.substring(i, i + 1)</span> in row-major order-the first row is filled from left to right, then the second row, and so on. When the test <span class="text-monospace">if (i &lt; str.length())</span> fails, the remaining matrix slots are filled with zeros, as in matrix I. Notice that if the number of slots in the matrix is less than the number of characters in <span class="text-monospace">str</span>, the method will quit without error before the entire string is processed, which is what happened for matrix III.

Question: 320
6.  Let  <span class="text-monospace">list</span> be an  <span class="text-monospace">ArrayList&lt;Integer&gt;</span> containing these elements: <pre class="monospace image_move"><span class="text-monospace">4 5 6 2 1</span> </pre> Which of the following statements will cause an error? (You may assume that integers added to the list will automatically be wrappedâauto-boxedâinto  <span class="text-monospace">Integer</span> objects.)
A. <span class="text-monospace">list.add(5);</span>  B. <span class="text-monospace">list.add(2, 4);</span>  C. <span class="text-monospace">Integer intOb = list.get(5);</span>  D. <span class="text-monospace">Object ob = list.add(5, 7);</span>  E. <span class="text-monospace">Integer x = list.set(3, 0);</span>
Correct Answer:  C
Explanation:
Answer: C   This statement will cause an <span class="text-monospace">IndexOutOfBoundsException</span> because there is no slot with index <span class="text-monospace">5</span>. Notice that choice D is correct: The size of the list will be adjusted to <span class="text-monospace">6</span>, and the <span class="text-monospace">Integer 7</span> will be added to the last slot, i.e., the slot with index <span class="text-monospace">5</span>.

Question: 321
7.  Refer to following method  <span class="text-monospace">insert</span>.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/comp_prin_3j.png"/>  Suppose that the element to be inserted has value  <span class="text-monospace">-8</span>. For which  <span class="text-monospace">list</span> will the method work as intended? <ol style="list-style-type:upper-roman">  8 4 0 -4   -2 -4 -6 -9   -1 -2 -4 -6  </ol>
A. I only  B. II only  C. III only  D. II and III only  E. I, II, and III
Correct Answer:  B
Explanation:
Answer: B   Note that the method will <i>fail</i> whenever <span class="text-monospace">element</span> is less than the last item in the list, because <span class="text-monospace">index</span> will be incremented to a value that is out of bounds. This will happen in lists I and III. Because <span class="text-monospace">-8</span> is greater than <span class="text-monospace">-9</span> (list II), the test in the method will be false, preventing an out-of-range error.

Question: 322
8.  Refer to the following declarations.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg158_01.png"/>  Which of the following correctly assigns the elements of the  <span class="text-monospace">birds</span> array to  <span class="text-monospace">birdList</span>? The final ordering need not be the same as in the  <span class="text-monospace">birds</span> array.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg158_02.png"/>
A. I only  B. II only  C. III only  D. I and III only  E. I, II, and III
Correct Answer:  A
Explanation:
Answer: A    The declaration of the <span class="text-monospace">birds</span> array makes the following assignments: <span class="text-monospace">birds[0] = "robin"</span>, <span class="text-monospace">birds[1] = "parrot"</span>, and <span class="text-monospace">birds[2] = "bluejay"</span>. The loop in segment I adds these values to <span class="text-monospace">birdList</span> in the same order. Segment II fails because <span class="text-monospace">birds</span> is an array and therefore can't use the <span class="text-monospace">get</span> method. The code also confuses the lists. Segment III, in its first pass through the loop, attempts to add <span class="text-monospace">birds[2]</span> to index position <span class="text-monospace">2</span> of the <span class="text-monospace">birdList</span>. This will cause an <span class="text-monospace">IndexOutOfBoundsException</span> to be thrown, since index positions <span class="text-monospace">0</span> and <span class="text-monospace">1</span> do not yet exist.

Question: 323
9.  Consider the following  <span class="text-monospace">Item</span> and <span class="text-monospace">Sale</span> classes:  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg159_01.png"/>  Which of the following correctly replaces  <span class="text-monospace">/* code to create a new Item */</span> in the  <span class="text-monospace">Sale</span> constructor to initialize the  <span class="text-monospace">itemList</span> array?
A. <span class="text-monospace">new Item(getDescription(), getPrice());</span>  B. <span class="text-monospace">new Item(itemDescription, itemPrice);</span>  C. <span class="text-monospace">new itemList(getDescription(), getPrice());</span>  D. <span class="text-monospace">new itemList(itemDescription, itemPrice);</span>  E. <span class="text-monospace">new itemList(theNumItems);</span>

Explanation:
Answer: B   For each <span class="text-monospace">i</span>, <span class="text-monospace">itemList[i]</span> is a new <span class="text-monospace">Item</span> object that must be constructed using the <span class="text-monospace">Item</span> constructor. Therefore, eliminate choices C, D, and E. Choice A is wrong because <span class="text-monospace">getDescription()</span> and <span class="text-monospace">getPrice()</span> are accessors for values <i>that already exist</i> for some <span class="text-monospace">Item</span> object.

Question: 324
10.  Consider the following  <span class="text-monospace">Item</span> and <span class="text-monospace">Sale</span> classes:  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg161_01.png"/>  Which represents correct  <span class="text-monospace">/* code to calculate amount */</span> in the  <span class="text-monospace">totalPaid</span> method?
A. <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg162_01.png"/>  B. <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg162_02.png"/>  C. <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg162_03.png"/>  D. <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg162_04.png"/>  E. <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg162_05.png"/>
Correct Answer:  C
Explanation:
Answer: C   To access the price for each <span class="text-monospace">Item</span> in the <span class="text-monospace">itemList</span> array, the <span class="text-monospace">getPrice()</span> accessor in the <span class="text-monospace">Item</span> class must be used, because <span class="text-monospace">price</span> is private to that class. This eliminates choices A and E. Choice B uses <span class="text-monospace">itemList</span> incorrectly: There's no <span class="text-monospace">getPrice</span> method for an array object. Choices D and E incorrectly declare a <span class="text-monospace">Sale</span> object. Question: 325
1.  Consider the <span class="text-monospace">insertionSort</span> method below, which does not always work as intended. The intention of the programmer is that the method will sort <span class="text-monospace">arr</span>, an array of integers, in descending order.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg163_01.png"/>  The programmer intends that after <span class="text-monospace">k</span> passes through the outer loop, elements <span class="text-monospace">arr[0], arr[1], . . . arr[k]</span> will be sorted with respect to each other, but not necessarily in their final sorted position. Each element in the unsorted part of the array will be moved to the left, until its insertion point is found in the sorted part of the array and then inserted into that slot.  The method doesnât work as intended in every case.  Which of the following arrays will cause an error, if passed as a parameter to the method above?
A. <span class="text-monospace">8, 2, 1, 6, 4</span>  B. <span class="text-monospace">6, 5, 4, 3, 2</span>  C. <span class="text-monospace">4, 4, 3, 4, 4</span>  D. <span class="text-monospace">2, 8, 1, 5, 3</span>  E. <span class="text-monospace">9, 7, 8, 9, 4</span>
Correct Answer:  D
Explanation:
Answer: D   The problem will occur whenever there’s an element in the array that is larger than the element in the first slot. Question: 326
2.  The elements of array  <span class="text-monospace">arr</span> are to be sorted in increasing order. Which represents the first step of a merge sort algorithm?
A. Find the smallest element in  <span class="text-monospace">arr</span> and swap it into  <span class="text-monospace">arr[0]</span>.  B. Compare  <span class="text-monospace">arr[0]</span> with  <span class="text-monospace">arr[1]</span> and, if necessary, shift and replace elements such that  <span class="text-monospace">arr[0]</span> is less than  <span class="text-monospace">arr[1]</span>.  C. Compare  <span class="text-monospace">arr[0]</span> with the middle element of  <span class="text-monospace">arr</span>,  <span class="text-monospace">arr[mid]</span>, and if  <span class="text-monospace">arr[0]</span> is less than  <span class="text-monospace">arr[mid]</span>, swap these elements.  D. Compare the first and last elements, and if the first is less than the last, swap these elements.  E. Break the array into roughly two equal halves.
Correct Answer:  E
Explanation:
Answer: E    Here's a recursive description of how merge sort works:   If there is more than one element in the array   Break the array into roughly two equal halves.   Merge sort the left half.   Merge sort the right half.   Merge the two subarrays into a sorted array.

Question: 328
4.  Consider the following program description.  A programmer plans to write a program that simulates a small card game (no more than four players). Each player will have a hand of ten cards, in which each card has a suit and a value. The game will involve either adding cards to a hand or discarding cards. The first player to have zero cards left in his hand is the winner. In the simulation, as the game is in progress, each player's hand is displayed on the screen.   The programmer plans to have a short class whose <span class="text-monospace">main</span> method has just two statements: <div class="s9-scrollable"> <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/qno33_01.png"> </img>   The <span class="text-monospace">Game</span> class will have several objects: a <span class="text-monospace">Display</span>, a <span class="text-monospace">Deck</span>, a <span class="text-monospace">Card</span>, and a <span class="text-monospace">PlayerGroup</span>. The <span class="text-monospace">PlayerGroup</span> will have a list of <span class="text-monospace">Player</span>s, and each <span class="text-monospace">Player</span> will have a <span class="text-monospace">Hand</span> of <span class="text-monospace">Card</span>s.  The relationship between the  <span class="text-monospace">Player</span> and  <span class="text-monospace">Hand</span> classes is an example of
A. inheritance  B. top-down design  C. information hiding  D. independent classes  E. composition
Correct Answer:  E
Explanation:
Answer: E   Composition is the <i>has-a</i> relationship. A Player <i>has-a</i> <span class="text-monospace">Hand</span>. Inheritance (choice A) is the <i>is-a</i> relationship, which doesn’t apply here. None of the choices B, C, or D apply here. Top-down design is a style of designing a program, not a relation between classes. Information hiding is the use of <span class="text-monospace">private</span> to restrict access; and <span class="text-monospace">Player</span> is <i>dependent</i> on <span class="text-monospace">Hand</span>, becasue a <span class="text-monospace">Player</span> has a <span class="text-monospace">Hand</span>.

Question: 329
5.  Consider the following program description.  A programmer plans to write a program that simulates a small card game (no more than four players). Each player will have a hand of ten cards, in which each card has a suit and a value. The game will involve either adding cards to a hand or discarding cards. The first player to have zero cards left in his hand is the winner. In the simulation, as the game is in progress, each player's hand is displayed on the screen.  The programmer plans to have a short class whose <span class="text-monospace">main</span> method has just two statements:  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/qno33_01.png"/>  The <span class="text-monospace">Game</span> class will have several objects: a <span class="text-monospace">Display</span>, a <span class="text-monospace">Deck</span>, a <span class="text-monospace">Card</span>, and a <span class="text-monospace">PlayerGroup</span>. The <span class="text-monospace">PlayerGroup</span> will have a list of <span class="text-monospace">Player</span>s, and each <span class="text-monospace">Player</span> will have a <span class="text-monospace">Hand</span> of <span class="text-monospace">Card</span>s.  Which is a reasonable data structure for a  <span class="text-monospace">Hand</span> object? Each hand starts with ten cards, and the number of cards can only go down. There should be a mechanism for removing a card, displaying a card, and for detecting a winning hand (no cards left in it).  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/comp_prin_3k.png"/>
A. I only  B. II only  C. III only  D. I and III only  E. I, II, and III
Correct Answer:  D
Explanation:
Answer: D   Data structure III conveniently stores a list of <span class="text-monospace">Card</span>s in which <span class="text-monospace">Card</span>s can easily be removed using the <span class="text-monospace">remove</span> method of <span class="text-monospace">ArrayList</span>. The array in data structure II allows for all cards in a deck to be represented (either in the <span class="text-monospace">Hand</span> or not); however, it doesn't provide a way to represent the suits and values of the cards themselves or to display a card. The array of <span class="text-monospace">Card</span> in data structure I may seem unsuitable because an array has fixed length. However, when a card is removed, it is easy to represent this by replacing that card with <span class="text-monospace">null</span> in that array slot.

Question: 332
8.  Consider the <span class="text-monospace">Name</span> class below.  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg171_01.png"/>  A full name in the <span class="text-monospace">Name</span> class consists of a first name, followed by a single blank, one middle initial, a period, another blank, and a last name. Some examples of full names are: <span class="text-monospace">John Q. Smith</span>, <span class="text-monospace">Camilla J. Hernandez</span>, <span class="text-monospace">Jo-Ann P. Green</span>, and <span class="text-monospace">Zach K. Teukolsky-Adams</span>.  Which is correct code for  <span class="text-monospace">/* code to get lastName */</span>? <ol style="list-style-type:upper-roman">  <span class="text-monospace">lastName = fullName.substring(index + 4);</span>   <span class="text-monospace">lastName = fullName.substring(index + 4, fullName.length());</span>   <span class="text-monospace">lastName = fullName.substring(firstName.length() + 4);</span>  </ol>
A. I only  B. II only  C. III only  D. I and II only  E. I, II, and III
Correct Answer:  E
Explanation:
Answer: E   They are all correct! One version of <span class="text-monospace">substring</span> has a single parameter, <span class="text-monospace">startIndex</span>. The method returns the substring that starts at <span class="text-monospace">startIndex</span> and goes to the end of the string. Segment I uses this version, starting at the position immediately following the second blank. Another version of <span class="text-monospace">substring</span> has two parameters, <span class="text-monospace">startIndex</span> and <span class="text-monospace">endIndex</span>. In this case, the <span class="text-monospace">substring</span> method returns the substring that starts at <span class="text-monospace">startIndex</span> and goes up to <span class="text-monospace">endIndex-1</span>. Segment II correctly uses this version. Segment III uses the single-parameter version of <span class="text-monospace">substring</span>, taking care to start at the correct position of <span class="text-monospace">fullName</span>. If the actual name were <span class="text-monospace">Pat C. Clark</span>, the last name starts at position <span class="text-monospace">7</span>, which can be obtained by:   length of <span class="text-monospace">firstName</span> + blanks + middle initial + period = 3 + 2 + 1 + 1 = 7

Question: 334
10.  The selection sort algorithm sorts an array  <span class="text-monospace">arr</span> of integers in ascending order as follows. <ol class="list-decimal" style="list-style-type:decimal">  Loop from  <span class="text-monospace">j = 0</span> to  <span class="text-monospace">j = arr.length-2</span> inclusive.   In each pass, swap  <span class="text-monospace">arr[j]</span> with the largest element in  <span class="text-monospace">arr[j+1]</span> through  <span class="text-monospace">arr[a.length-1]</span>.  </ol> A student writes the following code for this algorithm:  <img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg173_01.png"/>  The code doesn't work as intended. Which change should be made to fix it?
A. Change Line 3 to be:<img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg173_02a.png"/>  B. Change Line 6 to be:<img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg173_02b.png"/>  C. Change Line 5 to be:<img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg173_02c.png"/>  D. Change Line 10 to be:<img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg173_02d.png"/>  E. Change Line 8 to be:<img alt="" src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/computer-science-a/br23/pg173_02e.png"/>
Correct Answer:  C
Explanation:
Answer: C   For each pass through the loop, you want <span class="text-monospace"><span class="text-monospace">minIndex</span></span>, the index of the smallest element, to be initialized to the first element in the piece of array still to be sorted. The first element is determined by the current value of <span class="text-monospace"><span class="text-monospace">j</span></span>. Therefore, <span class="text-monospace"><span class="text-monospace">minIndex</span></span> must be initialized to <span class="text-monospace"><span class="text-monospace">j</span></span> for each pass through the outer loop. If <span class="text-monospace"><span class="text-monospace">minIndex</span></span> is always initialized to 0, which is the mistake the student made, the algorithm after the first pass through the outer loop will never find a smaller value than <span class="text-monospace">arr[0]</span> (which is the smallest value in the whole array). This means that the array will not get sorted. Choice A is wrong because you need <span class="text-monospace">arr.length-1</span> passes. If the loop goes from 0 to <span class="text-monospace">arr.length-1</span>, there will be one pass too many, and <span class="text-monospace">arr[<span class="text-monospace">k</span>]</span> will give an <span class="text-monospace">ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException</span> when <span class="text-monospace">k</span> equals <span class="text-monospace">j + 1</span>. Choice B fails in a similar way. If k equals <span class="text-monospace">arr.length</span>, <span class="text-monospace">arr[<span class="text-monospace">k</span>]</span> will give an <span class="text-monospace">ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException</span>. Choice D doesn't make sense. If <span class="text-monospace">arr[k]</span> is smaller than <span class="text-monospace">arr[<span class="text-monospace">minIndex</span>]</span>, then <span class="text-monospace"><span class="text-monospace">minIndex</span></span> must be set equal to <span class="text-monospace"><span class="text-monospace">k</span></span>. Choice E is wrong because you're searching for the smallest element. You therefore need to do a "less-than" test.
